<span id="freeTextContainer12216146356531215076">It is a just a tiny review for this one as sadly I did not enjoy my first try of one of Terry Pratchett's books. I did not gel with the writing style. The style was actually quite similar to that of Neil Gaiman's books and so unsurprisingly I had the same issues. The story itself was too ridiculous to take seriously and I felt like the characters were just inconsequential mouthpieces for the author to crack some jokes and offer a few witty insights on society. Now admittedly I liked the general </span>
  <span id="freeText12216146356531215076" style="display:none">It is a just a tiny review for this one as sadly I did not enjoy my first try of one of Terry Pratchett's books. I did not gel with the writing style. The style was actually quite similar to that of Neil Gaiman's books and so unsurprisingly I had the same issues. The story itself was too ridiculous to take seriously and I felt like the characters were just inconsequential mouthpieces for the author to crack some jokes and offer a few witty insights on society. Now admittedly I liked the general message and even laughed at the odd joke or witticism. The problem was that since the story and the characters were not taken very seriously by the author it was impossible for me to care about the happenings or become invested in the characters. <br /><br />Rating: 2.5 stars<br /><br />Audio Note: Stephen Briggs is a competent narrator who did a good job with the various voices and accents. That said, I was not a giant fan of the audio version as I've never been a fan of regional British accents. <br /><br /><br /></span>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67606852?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lightreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lightreads" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads">Lightreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=humor">humor</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67606852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3437125596051666110">Young sheep farmer's daughter begins training to be the witch of the chalk hills that she loves. She has the help of a lot of six-inch fairies with drinking problems and pointy swords, which is good because there's no school for learning witchery, unless you think of the whole world as the school.<br/><br/>Oh, <i>marvelous</i>. I read the three published books straight through everywhere I went, and I know I disturbed people by standing there <i>beaming</i> in the elevator. There may also have been bouncing.<br/><br/>These books</span>
  <span id="freeText3437125596051666110" style="display:none">Young sheep farmer's daughter begins training to be the witch of the chalk hills that she loves. She has the help of a lot of six-inch fairies with drinking problems and pointy swords, which is good because there's no school for learning witchery, unless you think of the whole world as the school.<br /><br />Oh, <i>marvelous</i>. I read the three published books straight through everywhere I went, and I know I disturbed people by standing there <i>beaming</i> in the elevator. There may also have been bouncing.<br /><br />These books! Hilarious, of course, as well they should be. But also rich and scary and sad. People die in these books, and children are faced with truths they shouldn't be, but it's all still fundamentally hopeful. But the thing I like the most is the magic. There is magic, you see, but that's not really what witching is about. Witching is about women, women being <i>so smart</i> and relying on each other and being midwives and caregivers and judges and priests and anything else that's needed. These are books about growing into power that are about the growing, not the power, which is so rare. So many fantasy books use magic as a shorthand for power – these books are about how they overlap, yes, but how they really aren't the same thing at all. <br /><br />*happy sigh* <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3437125596051666110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7915482057219758749">This was a book club read. I hadn't read anything by Terry Pratchett before and the novel certainly wasn't a genre that I've read a lot in. I enjoyed the world building that the author introduced and the delivery of the story. It was fast paced. I felt at heart that it was an adventure, a story of the "little guy" taking on the "big bad meanie" and triumphing against overwhelming odds. It's a theme that I often look for in the novels I read. In this case it was a nine year old girl called Tiffan</span>
  <span id="freeText7915482057219758749" style="display:none">This was a book club read. I hadn't read anything by Terry Pratchett before and the novel certainly wasn't a genre that I've read a lot in. I enjoyed the world building that the author introduced and the delivery of the story. It was fast paced. I felt at heart that it was an adventure, a story of the "little guy" taking on the "big bad meanie" and triumphing against overwhelming odds. It's a theme that I often look for in the novels I read. In this case it was a nine year old girl called Tiffany Aching.<br /><br />The characters overall were well presented, it was the little brother William who I found to be overly irritating though. I think that my favourite character overall was Miss Tick.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2565896854603028081">How can something be so funny, and at the same time so serious and deep? The whole story and Tiffany herself. She is so earnest, never surprised by the oddest things - wee free men popping up, witches and monsters appearing, the world needing to be saved…she takes all that in her stride. She questions things other people, even adults, take on face value, and she THINKS. About things in general, and also about her own thoughts and reactions.<br/><br/><i> “Yes! I'm <b>me</b>! I am careful and logical and I look up th</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2565896854603028081" style="display:none">How can something be so funny, and at the same time so serious and deep? The whole story and Tiffany herself. She is so earnest, never surprised by the oddest things - wee free men popping up, witches and monsters appearing, the world needing to be saved…she takes all that in her stride. She questions things other people, even adults, take on face value, and she THINKS. About things in general, and also about her own thoughts and reactions.<br /><br /><i> “Yes! I'm <b>me</b>! I am careful and logical and I look up things I don't understand! When I hear people use the wrong words, I get edgy! I am good with cheese. I read books fast! I <b>think</b>! And I always have a piece of string! That's the kind of person I am!”</i><br /><br />Tiffany learned from her grandmother that she has to protect those who cannot protect themselves:<br /><br /><i> “Them as can do has to do for them as can't. And someone has to speak up for them as has no voices."</i><br /><br />And she takes that responsibility seriously:<br /><br /><i> “Another world is colliding with this one,” said the toad. “There. Happy now? That’s what Miss Tick thinks. But it’s happening faster than she expected. All the monsters are coming back.”<br />“Why?”<br />“There’s no one to stop them.”<br />There was silence for a moment.<br />“There’s me,” said Tiffany. </i><br /><br />The Nac Mac Feegle, or wee free men, on the other hand, rarely think, they fight, steal and drink (not necessarily in that order). And they are hilarious!<br /><br /><i> “Whut's the plan, Rob?" said one of them. <br />"Okay, lads, this is what we'll do. As soon as we see somethin', we'll attack it. Right?"<br />This caused a cheer.<br />"Ach, 'tis a good plan," said Daft Wullie.”</i><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2627568489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7309746185532995008">I'm new around here. I've only visited Discworld twice now, but I'm loving it! I was surprised, because I don't often enjoy modern fantasy with its cynicism. I mean, if I'm reading fantasy, it's because I actually want the fantasy. I want to be immersed in a different. I don't want to be reminded of this one. Isn't that the draw? Isn't it why fantasy and escapism overtakes skepticism and becomes popular again after tragic events like 9/11? Whatever the case, for whatever reason, I'm digging the </span>
  <span id="freeText7309746185532995008" style="display:none">I'm new around here. I've only visited Discworld twice now, but I'm loving it! I was surprised, because I don't often enjoy modern fantasy with its cynicism. I mean, if I'm reading fantasy, it's because I actually want the fantasy. I want to be immersed in a different. I don't want to be reminded of this one. Isn't that the draw? Isn't it why fantasy and escapism overtakes skepticism and becomes popular again after tragic events like 9/11? Whatever the case, for whatever reason, I'm digging the Discworld stuff so far. For me, Pratchett hits the right note with books like these. </span>

<div id="review_3450946654" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3450946654" />
    <a title="Silvana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/666003-silvana"><img alt="Silvana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600533521p2/666003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3450946654?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvana" href="/user/show/666003-silvana">Silvana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780060824556" href="/book/show/13619112-the-wee-free-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=fyeahfantasy">fyeahfantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=2020-fantasy-novel-novella">2020-fantasy-novel-novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=sff-2020-reading-challenge">sff-2020-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=scribd">scribd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=growing-up">growing-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=series-i-abandoned">series-i-abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3450946654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13090304256099957162">One star is for the fantastic narration by Stephen Briggs. I am so glad I reread this.<br/><br/>To me, this is one of the best entries to the Discworld series, aside from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8__City_Watch__1_' title='Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8; City Watch #1) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Guards! Guards!</a>. So many good parts. Characters, oh Tiffany Aching is one of the best children characters I read. She's brave, resourceful, and so logical. She thinks. She thinks about her thinking! Yet the way she was described does not make her sounds annoying at all. She's just awesome and should be a role model for younger readers.<br/><br/>An</span>
  <span id="freeText13090304256099957162" style="display:none">One star is for the fantastic narration by Stephen Briggs. I am so glad I reread this.<br /><br />To me, this is one of the best entries to the Discworld series, aside from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8__City_Watch__1_" title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8; City Watch #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Guards! Guards!</a>. So many good parts. Characters, oh Tiffany Aching is one of the best children characters I read. She's brave, resourceful, and so logical. She thinks. She thinks about her thinking! Yet the way she was described does not make her sounds annoying at all. She's just awesome and should be a role model for younger readers.<br /><br />And Nac Mag Feegles, oh, I believe Pratchett described them as smurfs who watched too much Braveheart. They're more hilarious than that. Briggs really shine in voicing these feegles. <br /><br />So many gems....<br /><br />“If you trust in yourself. . .and believe in your dreams. . .and follow your star. . . you'll still get beaten by people who spent their time working hard and learning things and weren't so lazy.”<br /><br />"It didn't stop being magic just because you found out how it was done.”<br /><br />“And all the stories had, somewhere, the witch. The wicked old witch.<br />And Tiffany had thought: Where's the evidence?”<br /><br />“They can tak’ oour lives but they canna tak’ oour troousers!”<br /><br />Sigh. So good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13090304256099957162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_399823020" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/399823020" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/399823020?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552562904" href="/book/show/8478133-the-wee-free-men">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer399823020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3950084102540075294">OK, I’m going to start this review with some maths. No! Wait, don’t go. It’s going to be YA style maths and, well, it’s me… so it’ll be dead easy.<br/>Though before we begin, you can leave your payment in the basket just over there. Not vegetables. I want chocolate. Not got any? No worries…I’ll wait until you come back from the paper shop*.<br/>Back?<br/>Right:<br/><br/><strong>Hermione Granger + Mildred Hubble + Matilda Wormwood = Tiffany Aching.</strong><br/><br/>I’m almost tempted to just leave this review at that because, honestly, if you’re </span>
  <span id="freeText3950084102540075294" style="display:none">OK, I’m going to start this review with some maths. No! Wait, don’t go. It’s going to be YA style maths and, well, it’s me… so it’ll be dead easy.<br />Though before we begin, you can leave your payment in the basket just over there. Not vegetables. I want chocolate. Not got any? No worries…I’ll wait until you come back from the paper shop*.<br />Back?<br />Right:<br /><br /><strong>Hermione Granger + Mildred Hubble + Matilda Wormwood = Tiffany Aching.</strong><br /><br />I’m almost tempted to just leave this review at that because, honestly, if you’re not intrigued by that equation then I can’t recommend this book to you. Also, I can’t save your soul from eternal damnation.<br /><br />I’M KIDDING.<br /><em>Ish</em>.<br />But I won’t stop there because I like the sound of my voice or, you know, I like to see my typed words on a computer screen.<br /><br />I.loved.this.book.<br /><br />I have always said that when I’m rich and famous, I’m going to rent out a cottage in the middle of nowhere armed only with food, wine and Discworld books and just spend a week reading every single one of them from start to finish**. I’ve read a few of them (five, I think) and enjoyed them immensely but I think they are the kind of book you just need to immerse yourself in. And Discworld is so impeccably created that it’s the kind of world you need to spend a lot of time in, exploring it and learning its quirks and getting lost and finding your way out again. It probably helps if you’re slightly tipsy.<br />Even though Tiffany Aching’s adventures are set in Discworld and I understand they have a lot of overlapping characters, I believe that this could count as a standalone series. If you’ve read Discworld books before, you might get more of the jokes that have gone over my head but I honestly don’t think you’d need to have read any of them to get this story.<br />Actually, these books may be a great place to start.<br /><br />Sir Pratchett gives you just enough details about the setting to make sure you don’t get lost and I love that about him. I always think that Sir Pratchett has so many more ideas about the world that he keeps to himself so we as a reader only get to see about 75%  of what he has created. And I just love that restraint… because there would be nothing worse than if he was like ‘HAVE ALL THE DETAILS. MY IMAGINATION IS AMAZING. LOOK. LOOK. LOOK HOW BRILIANT I AM. YOU’RE NOT LOOKING AT THE BRILLIANCE.<br /><br />Because if you read a book like that you’d just get a headache and you’d probably need to lie down with a wet paper towel on your forehead. I just like the fact that even though he doesn’t share all the details, you know he's thought of everything and he's probably hiding them in his hat.<br /><br />I like to think that a Pratchett book is the reading equivalent of colouring in. Bear with me… His mind has created the most breathtakingly brilliant pictures, one that will take you a whole miserable Sunday afternoon to colour in because of all the rich detail and the intricacy. And then he just leaves a packet of pencil crayons on the table next to you and lets you go wild with it. You have free reign in Discworld and you’re encouraged to colour it in with whatever colours you want. As long as they are bright. And he’d probably encourage you to colour out of the lines in certain places too. He strikes me as that kind of guy.<br />Even if you know hardly anything about Sir Pratchett, you will probably be aware that he is funny. <em>Really</em> funny. I made the mistake of reading this book in the presence of other people and found myself having to explain about pointy horses and backwards moving sheep.<br />Needless to say, I got a few blank looks.<br /><em>”A pointy horse…IT’S HYSTERICAL.”</em> I would yell in their faces. <em>”A UNICORN IS A HORSE THAT ENDS IN A POINT!</em><br /><em>”Why are you shouting?”</em>  They would say, backing away slowly.<br /><em>“BECAUSE IT’S FUNNY!!!!!”</em><br /><em>“Stop using excessive punctuation.”</em><br /><em>“NEVER.”</em><br /><br />Trust me, it’s hysterical.<br />I just love his humour and I lovelovelove the fact that it hasn’t been dumbed down because this book is for… *gasps* *recoils in fear* <em>younger readers</em>. I can’t imagine any Pratchett fan being disappointed in these books.<br /><blockquote>“Are you listening?”<br />“Yes,” said Tiffany.<br />“Good. Now… if you trust in yourself…”<br />“Yes?”<br />“… and believe in you dreams…”<br />“Yes?”<br />“…and follow your star…” Miss Tick went on.<br />“Yes?”<br />“…you’ll still be beaten by people who spent <em>their</em> time working hard and learning things and weren’t so lazy. Goodbye.”</blockquote><br />LAUGHTER.<br /><br />But let’s talk about the main event: Tiffany. I can’t decide whether I want to be best friends with Tiffany Aching or actually be her when I grow up. She is intuitive, watchful and extremely smart. She’s the kind of girl who reads fairy tales but doesn’t want to be the princess, she wants to be the witch because <em>“where’s the evidence”</em> that they’re all wicked?<br />I can’t put into (um..intelligent) words how much I loved her so I’m going to give you an example of her brilliance:<br /><blockquote>“…did the book have any adventures for people who had brown eyes and brown hair? No, no, no… it was blond people with blue eyes and the redheads with green eyes who got the stories. If you had brown hair you were probably just a servant or a woodcutter or something. Or a dairymaid. Well, that was not going to happen, even if she <em>was</em> good at cheese. She couldn’t be the prince, and she’d never be a princess, and she didn’t want to be a woodcutter, so she’d be the witch and <em>know</em> things…”</blockquote><br />LOVE.HER. LOVE.THIS.BOOK. IT.MAKES.ME.TYPE.IN.BIZARRE.WAYS.<br /><br />READ.IT.<br /><br />*OK, I have just realised that this review will probably make no sense to people who haven’t read this book. But that’s not my fault. It’s clearly yours. So go and read it and then come back and tell me how brilliant and ingenious this review is. And…. ok, I guess the book is.<br /><br />**Well, ok… I’ll spend the first day trying to decide which order to read them in.<br /><br /><br /><br />You can read this review and lots of other exciting things on my blog, <a href="http://www.weartheoldcoat.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Wear the Old Coat.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3950084102540075294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5513724797725914074">The final pick for my kids' bookclub before they break for the summer. This is a complex and layered story that appealed to my 13 year old more than my 10 year old, although he might like it more at another time.<br/><br/>It isn't an easy read aloud with some of the accents (at least, not for me), but it is a pretty entertaining story.</span>

<div id="review_538408055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/538408055" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/538408055?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=awesome-girls">awesome-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=totally-awesome-book">totally-awesome-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=charming-mg">charming-mg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer538408055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4335089128727948482">I will start this post with another Old School Wednesdays’ confession: I only ever read one Terry Pratchett novel, Good Omens ages ago and that was only because he wrote that in collaboration with Neil Gaiman.<br/><br/>I know what you’re thinking right now: “CRIVENS! I can’t believe you haven’t read any Terry Pratchett till now, Ana.”<br/><br/>I KNOW, right? Anyway, the real problem with this course of action was of course, WHERE to start, given as how Pratchett has over 40 novels in the Discworld series alone. I h</span>
  <span id="freeText4335089128727948482" style="display:none">I will start this post with another Old School Wednesdays’ confession: I only ever read one Terry Pratchett novel, Good Omens ages ago and that was only because he wrote that in collaboration with Neil Gaiman.<br /><br />I know what you’re thinking right now: “CRIVENS! I can’t believe you haven’t read any Terry Pratchett till now, Ana.”<br /><br />I KNOW, right? Anyway, the real problem with this course of action was of course, WHERE to start, given as how Pratchett has over 40 novels in the Discworld series alone. I had on good authority that even though The Wee Free Men is Discworld book #30, it was a good place to begin as part of a four-book YA mini-series featuring 9-year-old Tiffany Aching. <br /><br />Tiffany is – as of this book – the current recipient of the newly-minted The Book Smugglers Award for Best Witch-To-Be on account of her perspicacity, courage, love for words, pride on her cheese-making skills as well as the ability to stand impervious and mostly unaffected by condescending adults, evil Queens, talking frogs and diminutive and outrageous, thievery blue men in kilts (otherwise known as Nac Mac Feegle or Pictsies [not to be confused with Pixies, if you please] or the Wee Free Men).<br /><br />This is the plot and Tiffany’s personality in a nutshell:<br /><br /> ”Another world is colliding with this one,” said the toad. “All the monsters are coming back.”<br /><br /> “Why?” said Tiffany.<br /><br /> “There’s no one to stop them.”<br /><br /> There was silence for a moment.<br /><br /> Then Tiffany said, “There’s me.”<br /><br />So! Armed with a frying pan (as we all know, a perfectly good weapon of choice as evidenced in Tangled), common sense, the memories of her Granny Aching, and an inordinate amount of Chutzpah, Tifanny embarks on a journey to Fairyland to save her kidnapped brother (whom she says she doesn’t really like all that much but he is hers and as such, she must get him back). And although ok, that setup is not necessarily unique, boy did I love this book.<br /><br />I loved Tiffany’s journey to Fairyland, as the two worlds collide and dreams and nightmares become intertwined with the real world and how the narrative itself seamlessly adapted to the ever-changing landscape that really reminded me of Diana Wynne Jones’ storytelling as well as Catherynne M. Valente’s recent Fairyland books. This ever-changing background and the stories-within-stories conceit also appears as Tiffany’s memories of her grandmother become clearer and clearer as she finally comes to understand what the stories about her really mean.<br /><br />The writing is just the type of writing that I love. It’s clever, it’s subtle, it presents valuable, meaningful themes and ideas without being didactic or dumbed down to readers, it has an amazingly clever and astute protagonist and on top of everything it.Is.Hilarious. The portrayal of the Wee Free Men is ostensibly funny (they are afraid of nothing! Except maybe of lawyers!) but the sense of humour is present in everything even when the text is discussing Important Things.<br /><br />Allow me to present a few choice quotes to better establish the above:<br /><br /> “All witches are selfish, the Queen had said. But Tiffany’s Third Thoughts said: Then turn selfishness into a weapon! Make all things yours! Make other lives and dreams and hopes yours! Protect them! Save them! Bring them into the sheepfold! Walk the gale for them! Keep away the wolf! My dreams! My brother! My family! My land! My world! How dare you try to take these things, because they are mine!”<br /><br />(I absolutely loved how the above quote both reinforces Tiffany’s age and how children can be selfish and self-centred without portraying those as bad things)<br /><br /> “ “Yes! I’m me! I am careful and logical and I look up things I don’t understand! When I hear people use the wrong words, I get edgy! I am good with cheese. I read books fast! I think! And I always have a piece of string! That’s the kind of person I am!” <br /><br />(How empowering is this?)<br /><br /> “The stories never said why she was wicked. It was enough to be an old woman, enough to be all alone, enough to look strange because you have no teeth. It was enough to be called a witch. If it came to that, the book never gave you the evidence of anything. It talked about “a handsome prince”… was he really, or was it just because he was a prince that people called handsome? As for “a girl who was as beautiful as the day was long”… well, which day? In midwinter it hardly ever got light! The stories don’t want you to think, they just wanted you to believe what you were told…” <br /><br />(To sum up: Tiffany wants to be a witch because there is a lack of actual evidence that they are actually wicked)<br /><br /> “ “Zoology, eh? That’s a big word, isn’t it.”<br /><br /> “No, actually it isn’t,” said Tiffany. “Patronizing is a big word. Zoology is really quite short.” <br /><br />(ha!)<br /><br />And finally, what might just be my favourite quote of the entire book:<br /><br /><br /> Are you listening?”<br /> “Yes,” said Tiffany.<br /> “Good. Now… if you trust in yourself…”<br /> “Yes?”<br /> “… and believe in you dreams…”<br /> “Yes?”<br /> “…and follow your star…” Miss Tick went on.<br /> “Yes?”<br /> “…you’ll still be beaten by people who spent their time working hard and learning things and weren’t so lazy. Goodbye.”<br /><br />Basically I spent my time reading The Wee Free Men by alternating between laughing my head off and earmarking thoughtful sequences. I’ve already made arrangements to get my grabby hands on the sequels. And maybe even other Terry Pratchett books (I hear Nation is most excellent).<br /><br />I am loving these Old School Wednesdays discoveries! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4335089128727948482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349494795" />
    <a title="Clouds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds"><img alt="Clouds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514641128p2/9374686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349494795?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clouds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clouds" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds">Clouds</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/833420.The_Wee_Free_Men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=pub-2000s">pub-2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=locus-ya">locus-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=discworld">discworld</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349494795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3606348378051035473"><a href='http://www.theaceofclouds.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2' rel='nofollow noopener'>Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=4' rel='nofollow noopener'>LOCUS Y-A</a> list.<br/><br/>I think I’ll always have a soft-spot for imaginative young-adult speculative fiction and as the good people at Locus did such a grand job with picking their Sci-Fi winners, I’ll trust them to single out some special y-a books too.</b><br/><br/>A toast f</span>
  <span id="freeText3606348378051035473" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.theaceofclouds.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=4" rel="nofollow noopener">LOCUS Y-A</a> list.<br><br>I think I’ll always have a soft-spot for imaginative young-adult speculative fiction and as the good people at Locus did such a grand job with picking their Sci-Fi winners, I’ll trust them to single out some special y-a books too.</b><br><br>A toast from Rob Anybody:<blockquote>
  <i>Ack! Crivens! What a bonnie wee hag, our wee hag is!<br><br>Terry Pratchett is the finest gonnagle this side of the chalk, ye ken? For a bigjob, as that. He’s got the knowing of the plot-weaving, and the unner-standin’ of the free dimensional characters. An tha’s a fine thing too, ‘cos them character dimensions d’nae be coming cheap! He knows his ups from his downs, his coos from his ships, and his hags from his quins, good an proper. An he give us all some licker, in silver thimbles too, like a real, right polite nob.<br><br>We Nac Mac Feegle ain’t known for our way with words – unless them words be fighting, stealing and drinking – but there are two ver’rae important words the kelda made me promise to remember if anyone ever asked about this book tha’ bigjob Terry has writ about our very own hag of the hills. It’s a kind of geas, ye ken? Ver’rae important. Those words be: REED IT.<br><br>Now, if ye dirty, great scunners are done – I’ll be getting back to the shindig.</i>
</blockquote>Thanks, Rob. I couldn’t have said it better myself. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Pratchett</a> is the King – as y’all should know by now. He is my Mr Reliable, and I’m kicking myself that I ever doubted it. For some reason, I thought I didn’t like this book. I know I started it, back in my student days, but I didn’t finish it. I can’t remember exactly why I didn’t finish the book, but for now let’s chalk it down to some kind of debauched, hedonistic rampage (involving drugs, sex, rock’n’roll and rhinos) – but the upshot was an assumption (and you know what they say about those). I assumed that if I didn’t finish it, it can’t have been all that good. Yes, I know, I’m dumber that Daft Wullie – no need to point it out.<br><br>When I finished my Locus Sci-Fi quest and decided to spread my wings, I took the Locus YA award into the fold. There were three <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/96852-discworld---tiffany-aching" rel="nofollow noopener">Tiffany Aching</a> books on this list – and I made number four an honorary member of the list ‘cos I’m a completionist like that. I wasn’t that excited about them due to the aforementioned daftness, so I started with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34492.Wintersmith" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Wintersmith</i>
</a>, book three in the series, because I happened to already own it. And y’know what, it’s great! But that’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326866835" rel="nofollow noopener">a different review</a>.<br><br>My point is... aw shucks, I have no idea any more!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/833420.The_Wee_Free_Men" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>
    <i>The Wee Free Men</i>
  </b>
</a> is excellent, through and through. Tiffany Aching is a great addition to the Discworld family and arguably the strongest stand-alone hero <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Sir Terry</a> has ever created. She certainly puts Rincewind to shame! She’s the heir to Granny Weatherwax, except she’s got a gang of mental fairies for a sidekick, instead of Nanny Ogg. She’s tough, smart, grounded and curious – everything an independent young heroine should be. And she knows that life ain’t like the storybooks, even when it seems like you’re in one (did anyone else smell metafic in the air?). <br><br>The story itself is really good – going on a quest into fairyland to rescue the Baron’s son – executed with the trademark flair, profundity and genre satire we’ve come to expect from the great man.<br><br>So why didn’t it get 5 stars? Gee, I’m not really sure. It certainly wasn’t miles away. Star ratings are always a gut reaction from me, and this is a solid 4-star. I can't point to any flaws, it just didn't give me that plastered-on grin that 5-star should.<br><br><b>After this I read: </b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349494816" rel="nofollow noopener">A Hat Full of Sky</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3606348378051035473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3293472705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3293472705" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10314106-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576969587p2/10314106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3293472705?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/10314106-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3293472705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11566833600488987657">My first introduction to Terry Prachtett was The Wee Free Men. What a great start into this wonderful author. His use of language, especially the speech of the Free Men (Nac Mac Feegle) is magnificently inventive. Though fantasy, one can easily picture small blue men existing in our homes and explaining the daily oddities of life. <br/>A must read for lovers of fantasy. No, a must read for anyone that enjoys a humorous and touching tale.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78316070" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78316070" />
    <a title="Steven Harbin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1283483-steven-harbin"><img alt="Steven Harbin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307406902p2/1283483.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78316070?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven Harbin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven Harbin" href="/user/show/1283483-steven-harbin">Steven Harbin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060012366" href="/book/show/233669.The_Wee_Free_Men">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78316070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12649522212663992967">I’m presently about half way through reading this marvelous little book. People have been recommending Mr. Pratchett’s work to me for years, and I must say that I’m sorry I took so long to finally start one of his books. I did read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12070.Good_Omens_The_Nice_and_Accurate_Prophecies_of_Agnes_Nutter__Witch' title='Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch</a> a while back, which he co-authored with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman' title='Neil Gaiman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Neil Gaiman</a>, and that book was excellent, but I was going through my NG phase at the time, and moved on to several of Gaiman’s books after reading GO. In retrosp</span>
  <span id="freeText12649522212663992967" style="display:none">I’m presently about half way through reading this marvelous little book. People have been recommending Mr. Pratchett’s work to me for years, and I must say that I’m sorry I took so long to finally start one of his books. I did read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12070.Good_Omens_The_Nice_and_Accurate_Prophecies_of_Agnes_Nutter__Witch" title="Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch</a> a while back, which he co-authored with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a>, and that book was excellent, but I was going through my NG phase at the time, and moved on to several of Gaiman’s books after reading GO. In retrospect, I should have pulled a TP novel into the mix at the time, but I am happy to be reading this one now. A “book friend” on the social network site Goodreads.com recommended TWFM to me and I must say, she was spot on regarding it. I started just this week and am already to page 158, which is pretty fast reading for me.<br /><br />The story of young witch-in-the-making Tiffany Aching and her allies, the Nac Mac Feegle (otherwise known as “The Wee Free Men” – think 6 inch high tattooed blue guys who could give the Fremen of Arrakis a run for their money in a fight) and her familiar on loan, a toad who seems to have been a lawyer who helped folks find grounds to sue in a previous life, and their quest to rescue Tiffany’s bothersome little brother from the Queen of Fairyland has been quite entertaining so far, and I’m looking forward to finishing it and checking out some of the other books in the series. I’ll give a full review after I finish it.<br /><br />After finishing this book, I'm a confirmed fan of Tiffany Aching, Terry Pratt, and Discworld. It was a good book to start reading the series, even though it is a young adult novel. Pratchett's sense of humor shines throughout, but at the same time there are definite serious things about this novel, for both young readers and older readers to ponder. Choices, what's real and what's important, all these things are explored by the main characters. I'm looking forward to more novels in the series, and I recommedn it to anyone who loves fantasy, young adult literature, humor, adventure, strong female characters and good reads in general.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12649522212663992967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1071686910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1071686910" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1071686910?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552551861" href="/book/show/1139152.The_Wee_Free_Men">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1071686910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1628311537957791265">What do a frying pan, a pair of oversized boots and some cheese have in common? They are part of one of THE best adventures on the Discworld!<br/><br/>Meet Tiffany, a 9-year-old girl from The Chalk. Her gran was a shepherdess (not only tending to sheep) until her death a few years ago and little Tiffany has never known anything other than churning butter and watching people (and dogs) herd sheep. Oh, and her sticky little brother demanding sweets.<br/>But one day, she is warned by some mysterious small blue cr</span>
  <span id="freeText1628311537957791265" style="display:none">What do a frying pan, a pair of oversized boots and some cheese have in common? They are part of one of THE best adventures on the Discworld!<br><br>Meet Tiffany, a 9-year-old girl from The Chalk. Her gran was a shepherdess (not only tending to sheep) until her death a few years ago and little Tiffany has never known anything other than churning butter and watching people (and dogs) herd sheep. Oh, and her sticky little brother demanding sweets.<br>But one day, she is warned by some mysterious small blue creatures and therefore able to defend the aforementioned sticky little brother with her trusted old frying pan. A <s>witch</s> <s>mystic woman</s> Miss Tick sees that and knows that Tiffany is ... special. But that kind of special is forbidden in the Chalk ... technically.<br>Nevertheless, Tiffany embarks on an adventure that introduces her not only to the Nac Mac Feegles' drinking/fighting/drinking-and-fighting but also to a talking toad, a snowy queen, dreams-come-true, some very misbehaving dogs and two persons dressed entirely in black.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1575237962i/28541405._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've heard that many people weren't all too happy with the introduction of such a young central character, which meant Sir Terry effectively entering YA territory. I am here to tell you it's all bullshit. Miss Tick, Tiffany, the Nac Mac Feegles ... they are all FANTASTIC. Hilarious, smart, lively, very thought-provoking (as we've come to expect from this author) and in one truly great setting!<br><br>This book is mostly about fairy tales and wishes that come true. But it is also about family - the ones we are born into as much as the ones we actually feel akin and belong to. It's about actually SEEING the world around you and caring for it. Deeply. It's about what really matters between people. It's about heart and being in the moment. Where and when it counts. And, of course, it's about Sir Terry's take on witches which is probably THE best version of magic I've ever read about.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1575237962i/28541406._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I didn't think it would be possible, but I think I might have a new favourite book in this series! Aye!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1628311537957791265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1953276164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1953276164" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/33384706-the-wee-free-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953276164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12318816149989168922"><i>The Wee Free Men</i> is the first book in the <i>Tiffany Aching</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. Calling it “young adult” might be a stretch since the protagonist is nine and I thought the story seemed suitable for a younger audience. On the other hand, as with many children protagonists, she probably behaved as if she were older than a typical nine-year-old. In any case, the story was entertaining enough for an adult to enjoy and I did enjoy it quite a bit.<br/><br/>The story is set in a small farming community, where w</span>
  <span id="freeText12318816149989168922" style="display:none"><i>The Wee Free Men</i> is the first book in the <i>Tiffany Aching</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. Calling it “young adult” might be a stretch since the protagonist is nine and I thought the story seemed suitable for a younger audience. On the other hand, as with many children protagonists, she probably behaved as if she were older than a typical nine-year-old. In any case, the story was entertaining enough for an adult to enjoy and I did enjoy it quite a bit.<br /><br />The story is set in a small farming community, where witchcraft is frowned upon. Tiffany, whose late grandmother was possibly a witch, seems to have some skills in that area herself. Those skills are put to the test when creatures from another world start showing up near Tiffany’s home. Without any other witches living nearby, she must try to deal with things herself until more experienced witches can arrive. Fortunately, she does have a ‘little’ help in the meantime.<br /><br />Tiffany Aching is a good character, easy to sympathize with and root for. I also really enjoyed the Nac Mac Feegles who are the “Wee Free Men” referenced in the title. They, and to some extent the talking toad, were a lot of fun. There wasn’t as much satire and puns in this book, but it did have some light humor. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12318816149989168922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1241728326" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1241728326" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2435876637414460548">And now I'm at the point of stacking reviews :)<br/><br/>Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2019.<br/><br/>The below review is from an audiobook listen a few years ago. This time around I did it in print, and even though I can nearly recite it at this point, after reading the brilliant <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47989.Night_Watch__Discworld___29__City_Watch___6_' title='Night Watch (Discworld, #29; City Watch, #6) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Night Watch</a> I just had to keep going.<br/><br/>Interestingly this was my first time rereading after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22886868.The_Shepherd_s_Crown__Discworld___41__Tiffany_Aching___5_' title='The Shepherd's Crown (Discworld, #41; Tiffany Aching, #5) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shepherd's Crown</a> and I found the parallels fascinating. As much as this is a book about Tiffany und</span>
  <span id="freeText2435876637414460548" style="display:none">And now I'm at the point of stacking reviews :)<br /><br />Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2019.<br /><br />The below review is from an audiobook listen a few years ago. This time around I did it in print, and even though I can nearly recite it at this point, after reading the brilliant <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47989.Night_Watch__Discworld___29__City_Watch___6_" title="Night Watch (Discworld, #29; City Watch, #6) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Watch</a> I just had to keep going.<br /><br />Interestingly this was my first time rereading after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22886868.The_Shepherd_s_Crown__Discworld___41__Tiffany_Aching___5_" title="The Shepherd's Crown (Discworld, #41; Tiffany Aching, #5) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shepherd's Crown</a> and I found the parallels fascinating. As much as this is a book about Tiffany understanding the core of herself, it's about grief for her grandmother and there's a parallel there in the final book of the series that makes other elements of that plot important too.<br /><br />Anyway ... brilliant book, master at the peak of his art and trying something new and difficult ... blah, blah.<br /><br />-------------------------------<br /><br />This review is from my latest "read" of this beloved book, this time by listening to the abridged audio recording narrated by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/34204.Tony_Robinson" title="Tony Robinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tony Robinson</a>. I have previously listened to the unabridged audio narrated by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19439.Stephen_Briggs" title="Stephen Briggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen Briggs</a> and I have read the text editions at least twice.<br /><br />It is, of course, brilliant. In my opinion, the Tiffany Aching books are the pinnacle of a long career. In this one we meet Tiffany at 9 years old as she begins the path of a witch as she deals with that and her deep grief for her grandmother. She meets her greatest allies, the Nac Mac Feegle, the small blue men, pictsies that were kicked out of fairyland on charges of being drunk and disorderly. And she takes on her first foe, the Queen of the Elves.<br /><br />In terms of this recording Robinson does a good job. I much prefer Stephen Briggs, but I was in a vehicle with people who hadn't read this before and they appreciated it. In terms of it being an abridged edition, the cutting didn't seem egregious although I did end up missing a few elements.<br /><br />If you haven't read it yet, you should. If you want to try Pratchett and are daunted by the numbers in this series, this is a good starting point with Pratchett as his peak. The two characters from the main series are introduced well here and not until the end of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2435876637414460548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_16838425" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16838425" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/222412-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561312270p2/222412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16838425?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/222412-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Beverly by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/222511-kim">Kim</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16838425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5934697652767695454">From the review on my blog: <br/>Pratchett takes all sorts of fairy tales and children's stories--including one of my faves, Peter Pan--and mashes them into his own tale about Tiffany, a nine-year-old witch in training. Tiffany is gutsy, smart (she's got First Sight and Second Thoughts; I need to develop both myself!), and ethical. In the same way I wanted to be Jo March when I first read Little Women, I can imagine any girl selecting Tiffany as a role model.<br/><br/>Pratchett never writes down to his reader;</span>
  <span id="freeText5934697652767695454" style="display:none">From the review on my blog: <br />Pratchett takes all sorts of fairy tales and children's stories--including one of my faves, Peter Pan--and mashes them into his own tale about Tiffany, a nine-year-old witch in training. Tiffany is gutsy, smart (she's got First Sight and Second Thoughts; I need to develop both myself!), and ethical. In the same way I wanted to be Jo March when I first read Little Women, I can imagine any girl selecting Tiffany as a role model.<br /><br />Pratchett never writes down to his reader; instead, he seems fascinated by the world he's created, and that fascination comes through to the reader. He loves his characters, and renders them with precision and care. He has created a number of strong females in this book, and lord knows we need more of those in kids' lit. The author's sense of play comes through, and the wisdom he grants Granny Aching informs the novel throughout with such gems as Tiffany's observation that Granny Aching used words "as though they cost money" and Tiff's own realization that<br /><br />"Yes! I'm me! I am careful and logical and I look up things I don't understand! When I hear people use the wrong words, I get edgy! I am good with cheese. I read books fast! I think! And I always have a piece of string! That's the kind of person I am!"<br /><br />I don't know about you, but Tiffany's just the sort of girl I wanted to be. And Granny Aching? Well, she's certainly a paragon among women.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5934697652767695454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_106343127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106343127" />
    <a title="Althea Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann"><img alt="Althea Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106343127?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385605335" href="/book/show/833499.The_Wee_Free_Men">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106343127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14916817956493489383">This was marketed as a Discworld novel for 'younger readers,' but I<br/>found the story and style to be no more (or less) juvenile than that<br/>of any of Pratchett's other books. It's the 30th Discworld book, and<br/>the first to feature the character Tiffany Aching (although i was<br/>already familiar with her from reading 'Wintersmith' - I've never<br/>tried to read Pratchett in order.)<br/>Nine-year-old Tiffany's baby brother is kidnapped by the Queen of the<br/>Elves - an antagonist who spreads winter where ever she goes. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText14916817956493489383" style="display:none">This was marketed as a Discworld novel for 'younger readers,' but I<br />found the story and style to be no more (or less) juvenile than that<br />of any of Pratchett's other books. It's the 30th Discworld book, and<br />the first to feature the character Tiffany Aching (although i was<br />already familiar with her from reading 'Wintersmith' - I've never<br />tried to read Pratchett in order.)<br />Nine-year-old Tiffany's baby brother is kidnapped by the Queen of the<br />Elves - an antagonist who spreads winter where ever she goes. The<br />brother, Wentworth, is a pain-in-the-butt, continually sticky brat,<br />but Tiffany is determined to rescue him. It's lucky that Tiffany is<br />the granddaughter of a witch, and definitely has inherited the talent<br />to realize her aspirations of becoming one herself. Also on her side,<br />somewhat mysteriously, she seems to have a horde of miniature Scotmen<br />- the Nac Mac Feegle. Although the premise is certainly not one we've<br />never heard before, the talents of Pratchett make the story both<br />original and hilarious. The tribe of the Nac Mac Feegle (troublemaking<br />Pictsies!) are definitely one of his best inventions. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14916817956493489383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1138082818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138082818" />
    <a title="lucky little cat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38160628-lucky-little-cat"><img alt="lucky little cat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600336662p2/38160628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138082818?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lucky little cat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lucky little cat" href="/user/show/38160628-lucky-little-cat">lucky little cat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060012366" href="/book/show/233669.The_Wee_Free_Men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=kickass-heroines">kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=it-s-funny">it-s-funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=and-i-can-t-get-it-out-of-my-head">and-i-can-t-get-it-out-of-my-head</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=4-anglophiles">4-anglophiles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=books-i-ve-read-5-or-more-times">books-i-ve-read-5-or-more-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=deserves-more-popularity">deserves-more-popularity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=kid-lit">kid-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=it-s-just-a-fantasy">it-s-just-a-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138082818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9001868254763901142">One of Terry Pratchett's best Discworld heroines, the acidly unflappable Susan Sto Helit, explains her life's philosophy: <b>"In this world, after everyone panics, there's always got to be someone to tip the wee out of the shoe."*</b> And get on with things already, is the clear implication. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0765458/?ref_=ttmi_tt' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1599703076i/30085308._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <i>Who else besides a very young Michelle Dockery would play Susan Sto Helit?</i>
</a><br/><br/>It's one of my favorite descriptions of a certain kind of understated, undersung, common-sense heroism. And Susan Sto Helit would </span>
  <span id="freeText9001868254763901142" style="display:none">One of Terry Pratchett's best Discworld heroines, the acidly unflappable Susan Sto Helit, explains her life's philosophy: <b>"In this world, after everyone panics, there's always got to be someone to tip the wee out of the shoe."*</b> And get on with things already, is the clear implication. <br><br><a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0765458/?ref_=ttmi_tt" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1599703076i/30085308._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <i>Who else besides a very young Michelle Dockery would play Susan Sto Helit?</i>
</a><br><br>It's one of my favorite descriptions of a certain kind of understated, undersung, common-sense heroism. And Susan Sto Helit would certainly recognize <i>Wee Free Men</i>'s nine-year-old Tiffany Aching as a kindred spirit. <b>Like Susan, Tiffany can sense trouble brewing from a mile away (and six months in advance).</b> If only Sir Terry had gotten to write the series installment where the two young witches meet, say <i>Discworld #142.</i><br><br>When Tiffany marches out to fight what-might-just-possibly-be-monsters, she's armed only with a cast-iron frying pan and a strong sense of outraged decency: how <i>dare</i> such things attack <i>her</i> village? <br><br><a href="https://www.kenleslie.co.uk/photo_12487136.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1599703076i/30085309._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <i>"The Chalk" stands in for Pratchett's home village Broad Chalke and the Chalke Valley near Salisbury.</i>
</a><br><br><b>The Tiffany Aching series can also be surprisingly sweet and literally pastoral.</b> We get to eavesdrop a little on Tiffany's family and their sheep-farm on "the Chalk." And we get to eavesdrop <i>a lot</i> on Tiffany's memories of her beloved Granny Aching, a taciturn, infinitely practical woman who'd been her small community's moral backbone.** After only a few of these brief flashbacks, we understand that we are seeing the very beginnings of Tiffany's coming to grips with her own grief. <br><br><b>The series will undoubtedly be too twee for some readers. </b> Tiffany's aided and abetted by a small clan of (small) blue "pictsies," the Feegles, and a few readers <i>I</i> know have been turned right off by these varmints, who are a kilt-wearin', swearin', hard-drinkin', hard-fightin', heavily-Scotch-brogued crew. <br><br><b>I personally like (most) twee, and I can reliably adore Pratchett's brand of it. I like the Feegles for two reasons. First, they share Tiffany's demanding work ethic. Their language is <i>stuffed</i> with dismissive names for loafers and liars: spavies, mudlins, scunners, scuggans, and, my personal favorite denunciation, "wee streak of uselessness."<br><br>Second, how could I help but adore characters who say things like, ‘Ye’ve got ta’ let me go sooner or later, ye big ’natomy!’. . . And then ye’re gonna get sich a kickin’!’***</b><br><br>And honestly, my favorite part of the Tiffany Aching series is the part <i>after</i> the adventure's over when Tiffany has to take stock and figure out what in the world comes next. Those final chapters aren't long, but they're plenty deep. <br>__________<br><br>*From Pratchett's <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6565863.Thief_of_Time__Discworld___26_" title="Thief of Time (Discworld, #26) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Thief of Time</a>.</i><br><br>**<i>"Speak up for those who don’t have voices,</i> [Granny] always said," Tiffany reports about the roots of her own philosophy. <br><br>***Lines a Feegle delivers to the character Death in <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618145.A_Hat_Full_of_Sky__Discworld___32_" title="A Hat Full of Sky (Discworld, #32) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">A Hat Full of Sky</a>
</i>. Death answers <i>back,</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["I WAS NOT EXPECTING A NAC MAC FEEGLE TODAY, said Death. OTHERWISE I WOULD HAVE WORN PROTECTIVE CLOTHING, HA HA." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><br><b>My erstwhile review, which I'm too lazy to edit and too vain to delete:</b><br><br>This book and its sequels are permanently rooted in my family's culture, so that we go around using a fake brogue to say to each other, "Ooh, when you put me down, yer gonna get <i>such</i> a kickin'!!"<br><br>We also occasionally try to talk in all caps, but lack the gravit-arse to pull it off properly.<br><br>Thank you, Sir Terry Pratchett. Life would be so plain without your work.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9001868254763901142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
